  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cd91287f-2fe9-43e6-867d-c646d0ac3e32'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer14575575767986538295"><p>A century before A GAME OF THRONES, two unlikely heroes wandered Westeros…</p><p>A KNIGHT OF THE SEVEN KINGDOMS compiles the first three official prequel novellas to George R.R. Martin’s ongoing masterwork, A SONG OF ICE AND FIRE.</p><p>Before Tyrion Lannister and Podrick Payne there was Dunk and Egg.</p><p>A young, naïve but courageous hedge knight, Ser Duncan the Tall towers above his rivals</p></span>
  <span id="freeText14575575767986538295" style="display:none"><p>A century before A GAME OF THRONES, two unlikely heroes wandered Westeros…</p><p>A KNIGHT OF THE SEVEN KINGDOMS compiles the first three official prequel novellas to George R.R. Martin’s ongoing masterwork, A SONG OF ICE AND FIRE.</p><p>Before Tyrion Lannister and Podrick Payne there was Dunk and Egg.</p><p>A young, naïve but courageous hedge knight, Ser Duncan the Tall towers above his rivals – in stature if not experience. Tagging along with him is his diminutive squire, a boy called Egg – whose true identity must be hidden from all he and Dunk encounter: for in reality he is Aegon Targaryen, and one day he will be king. Improbable heroes though they be, great destinies lie ahead for Dunk and Egg; as do powerful foes, royal intrigue, and outrageous exploits.</p><p>A KNIGHT OF THE SEVEN KINGDOMS brings together for the first time the first three official prequel novellas to George R.R. Martin’s ongoing masterwork, A SONG OF ICE AND FIRE, set in an age when the Targaryen line still holds the Iron Throne, and the memory of the last dragon has not yet passed from living memory.</p><p>Featuring more than 160 illustrations by Gary Gianni, one of the finest fantasy artists of our time, this beautiful volume will transport readers to the world of the Seven Kingdoms in an age of bygone chivalry.</p></span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/4321783-kim">Kim</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">There was sexual content in the book. It's not a book for kids at all, and for teens only if you're comfortable having them read about brothels, plays<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">There was sexual content in the book. It's not a book for kids at all, and for teens only if you're comfortable having them read about brothels, plays on the word "pussy", teens being caught in the middle of sex in a kitchen, and people undressing the bride and copping feels on the way to her bedding.<br /><br />I used to teach high school English and I'm not ignorant of what teens get up to by any means, but I'd be uncomfortable and would not let my own teen-aged children read it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/537378-when-would-it-be-best-to-read-these-3">When would it be best to read these 3 short stories? Before or after the Song of ice &amp; fire series? Please no spoilers!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_537378'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18635622-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/537378-when-would-it-be-best-to-read-these-3">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/537378-when-would-it-be-best-to-read-these-3">See all 16 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/3694251-waldo-varjak"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1421404877i/3694251._UY100_CR10,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/3694251-waldo-varjak">Waldo Varjak</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I believe the author wrote these short stories concurrent to the writing of his Song of Ice & Fire perhaps using the opportunity in fewer word count t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I believe the author wrote these short stories concurrent to the writing of his Song of Ice &amp; Fire perhaps using the opportunity in fewer word count to embellish and buttress his own knowledge and understanding of the world within which he writes by working in elements of medieval period research. As I suspect for the aurthor, these stories can enhance the reader's appreciation of the larger Song. <br /><br />They are stand alone stories. As such, they are self contained. Everything you need to know is within the story itself. This is not fan fiction.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_2493317145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2493317145" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2493317145?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007507672" href="/book/show/23306321-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">ASOIAF fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2493317145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6334723988921444786"><b><i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> is a great prequel compilation with superb production value.</b><br/><br/>I’m currently in the middle of collecting all the books within <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i> in hardcover format. Honestly speaking, unlike <i>The World of Ice and Fire</i> and <i>Fire and Blood</i>, I didn’t have a lot of interest in reading this book; I treated it as a completionist read or a diversion while I wait for the release for <i>The Winds of Winter</i>. This is also why I'm happy that this book ended up being such a pleasa</span>
  <span id="freeText6334723988921444786" style="display:none"><b><i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> is a great prequel compilation with superb production value.</b><br><br>I’m currently in the middle of collecting all the books within <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i> in hardcover format. Honestly speaking, unlike <i>The World of Ice and Fire</i> and <i>Fire and Blood</i>, I didn’t have a lot of interest in reading this book; I treated it as a completionist read or a diversion while I wait for the release for <i>The Winds of Winter</i>. This is also why I'm happy that this book ended up being such a pleasant surprise for me.<br><br><b>Picture: One of the interior illustrations by Gary Gianni.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549113694i/27005156._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> is a compilation of the three prequel novellas in <i>The Tales of Dunk and Egg</i> series by George R. R. Martin. It’s a prequel to <i>A Song of Ice and Fire</i> and the story starts about a century before the events in <i>A Game of Thrones</i>. Ser Duncan the Tall (Dunk) and Egg were simply fascinating to read. Starting from their encounter in <i>The Hedge Knight</i>, each novella continues to develop their characterizations and relationship more. Unlike the main series, the tone of this much more light-hearted. The knights in Westeros are often times asshole, coward, and despicable. This has been proven countless times throughout the main series. Dunk is a different kind of knight; honorable, courageous, naïve, and awkward. The friendship between Dunk and Egg was subtle and I found the unlikely harmony in their interaction to be funny, heartwarming, and highly engaging. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“A great battle is a terrible thing," the old knight said, "but in the midst of blood and carnage, there is sometimes also beauty, beauty that could break your heart.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I don’t have really have a lot of things to say regarding this collection because of the short length. This book is 360 pages long and there are more than 160 gorgeous illustrations done by Gary Gianni that filled the pages of this book; they made the book feel shorter but at the same time they totally enhanced my reading experience to be much more atmospheric. I can’t help it, I’m a sucker for a novel with interior illustrations; in my opinion this book has a terrific production value.<br><br><b>Picture: One of the interior illustrations by Gary Gianni.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549113694i/27005155._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I enjoyed reading all the three novellas. My rating for thenovellas: <b>4.5/5 stars</b> for <i>The Hedge Knight</i>, <b>3.5/5 stars</b> for <i>The Sworn Sword</i>, and <b>4/5 stars</b> for <i>The Mystery Knight</i>. Overall, I think fans of the main series will have a wonderful time with this book. Martin once again shows that even in a novella format, he’s still a writer with immense talent at characterizations and world-building. <i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> offers a glimpse of the rich history behind Westeros through the eyes of the finely written duo: Dunk and Egg. I can’t believe I’m saying this—especially knowing that the main series is in limbo status—but I’m really looking forward to the continuation of the duo's story and how it all eventually connects to the main series.<br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9780345533487/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/02/02/a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6334723988921444786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1421953382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421953382" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421953382?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007507672" href="/book/show/23306321-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=4-star-reads">4-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=children-of-all-ages">children-of-all-ages</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421953382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11802579346245929074">Now I’ve of course read these before, but I simply had to get this edition for the illustrations. They did wonders and capturing the story; they almost brought new life to it. So, it was money well spent and, as an added bonus, I had an excuse to read these short stories again!<br/><br/><b> A memorable friendship </b><br/><br/>Dunc and Egg make a wonderful pair. Ser Duncan is not only a knight in name, but also one in deed. This is something increasingly rare in the seven kingdoms. There are few true knights and even fewe</span>
  <span id="freeText11802579346245929074" style="display:none">Now I’ve of course read these before, but I simply had to get this edition for the illustrations. They did wonders and capturing the story; they almost brought new life to it. So, it was money well spent and, as an added bonus, I had an excuse to read these short stories again!<br><br><b> A memorable friendship </b><br><br>Dunc and Egg make a wonderful pair. Ser Duncan is not only a knight in name, but also one in deed. This is something increasingly rare in the seven kingdoms. There are few true knights and even fewer when the events of <i> A Song of Ice and Fire</i> take place. He is really part of a dying breed in Westeros. So, he is honourable and strong; he is just and kind: he is everything a knight should be. However, he is not at all wise; he’s <i>"Dunk the lunk, thick as a castle wall."</i> I suppose not everybody can have everything. We all have our weaknesses, and this is where the young prince Aegon Targaryen comes in to balance the friendship. <br><br><i>"A hedge knight must hold tight to his pride. Without it, he was no more than a sellsword" </i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1445449377p8/1334009.jpg" width="440" height="776" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Egg is still a boy, though he has a fully developed mind that even the Maesters shall envy. He tempers Ser Duncan’s wrath, guiding him to choose the best course of action. Indeed he has the mind that Duncan lacks. However, for all his intelligence, he still has a whole world to see and understand; he still needs to develop his wisdom. By being Duncan’s squire, he gets to see honour and decency; he begins to understand how people work, and how best to defeat them; he learns that it can be achieved through words as well as deeds. <br><br>The two embark on some interesting adventures. Their first (<i>The Hedge Knight </i>) is by far my favourite. It depicts the pair’s first meeting, and they discover how important them coming together was. Dunc changes the fate of the Seven Kingdoms. The two only met by chance. Their actions lead to the altercation of who is to be the next King. So, it’s all rather far reaching stuff. The second story (<i> The Sworn Sword</i>) didn’t quite work for me and felt a little flat in all. The third (<i> The Mystery Knight</i>) made up for it, though, with its character defining moments. <br><br><i>"Kings rise and fall, Dunk thought, and cows and smallfolk go about their business."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1445449400p8/1334010.jpg" width="400" height="248" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I did have a lot of fun reading these through again, and I think that they really are required reading for fans of the series. In addition to this, the illustration did help a lot to capture the essence of the story. This isn’t the first time I’ve said this in a review now, but I do hope that this book marks the last thing that is (re)published before the release of <i> A Winds of Winter. </i> It’s starting to get a little ridiculous now, and the afterward didn’t help things: ol’ Georgy suggests that there are more tales from the pair to come. <br><br>I hope he means after <i> A Song of Ice and Fire!</i> But, that’s beside the point, this was still fun to read. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446995790i/16941203._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="636" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11802579346245929074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2755714806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2755714806" />
    <a title="James Tivendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale"><img alt="James Tivendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605206526p2/10282461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2755714806?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James Tivendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James Tivendale" href="/user/show/10282461-james-tivendale">James Tivendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26258847-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10282461-james-tivendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2755714806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer490261515479597460">A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms is a collection of three novellas that are set a generation or two before the events of A Song and Ice and Fire. In the third person perspective, we follow Dunk or as he tailors himself - Ser Duncan the Tall. The first narrative is named The Hedge Knight and we are presented to our protagonist as he is burying his former mentor for whom he used to squire. It's a touching start, and an interesting introduction to Dunk. He is planning to go to a tourney in Ashford an</span>
  <span id="freeText490261515479597460" style="display:none">A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms is a collection of three novellas that are set a generation or two before the events of A Song and Ice and Fire. In the third person perspective, we follow Dunk or as he tailors himself - Ser Duncan the Tall. The first narrative is named The Hedge Knight and we are presented to our protagonist as he is burying his former mentor for whom he used to squire. It's a touching start, and an interesting introduction to Dunk. He is planning to go to a tourney in Ashford and at a crossroads inn he meets Egg, who he assumes is a stable boy. This boy decides to follow Dunk without permission, wanting to squire for him, and eventually it transpires that he is of royal blood and would eventually become Aegon V, protector of the realm, etc... He is the brother of Aemon Targaryen who becomes Lord Commander of the Night's Watch and at this time Bloodraven is the Hand of the King. This is the gentleman who becomes the three-eyed-raven. <br /><br />"Dunk the lunk, thick as a castle wall." <br /><br />At 17 years old, almost 7-foot-tall, strong and with weight and reach in his favour, Dunk is a formidable Hedge Knight. Essentially, he is a Knight who travels throughout the 7 Kingdoms doing jobs he deems true and honourable for coin. Dunk is as true and decent as any Knight you would have read about in A Song of Ice and Fire and there is a fan theory that Brienne is a descendant of his and I can totally believe that. We are presented the tale from his mind and he talks himself down over explaining his stupidity. I never really saw him as being dim. He can't read, he has never kissed a girl and he doesn't really have people skills but some of the supporting cast and villains who can and have done these come across as more vile and horrid when reflected against Dunk's honesty, loyalty and general goodheartedness. <br /><br />Egg is a pretty amazing character. Even though he has Targaryen purple eyes he shaves his head so his gold/silver hair doesn't make it completely obvious regarding his lineage. And he has a silly straw hat! He is described as being as wise as a maester but still only 10. He knows the history of the majority of the nation's houses and can name who someone is just by seeing the paintwork on their shields. He is also quick of tongue sometimes to his detriment, especially when these 3 novella's often discuss the Targaryan Blackfyre rebellion and hints at seeds of which are still spread throughout the land. I read this after I read GRRM's Fire and Blood and the knowledge I gained regarding the Targaryan's there did enhance my experience although it isn't truly necessary to read in that order. I think this could be thoroughly enjoyed by someone who has not yet read the main series. It's not all pretty and it does feature numerous deaths, violence and backstabbing but from Dunk's perspective, these stories present a lot more hope and goodness than we are accustomed to from a typical Westeros tale. <br /><br />Anyone reading this who knows me personally will be aware that I have had one of the worst weeks of my life. If I believed in guardian angels I would think that mine made me pick up this book at this time instead of the other 1000 books on my to-be-read list. This story was exactly what I needed. Interesting, funny, about friendship with elements of trust, mystery and excitement. I've always looked down upon reviewers who rate a book 6/5 as I think it makes no sense. After this scenario and how this book has helped me recover then this is the closest I will ever get to giving that rating. It's the best novel I've read this year and I can't wait to read about more Dunk and Egg.</span>
  <a data-text-id="490261515479597460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Pasta blanda 9780008238094" href="/book/show/34835283-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13488018983228950124"><i> “Dunk the lunk, thick as a castle wall.” </i><br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed these three novellas. It was great to return to Westeros, one hundred years before the events of ASoIaF. We follow Dunk, a hedge knight risen up by an old knight with no heirs. He gets himself a squire named Egg, who unbeknownst to him is Prince Aegon - one of the Targaryen Princes. <br/><br/><i> “Oak and iron guard me well, or else I’m dead and doomed to hell.” </i><br/><br/>We see Dunk get himself into all kinds of scrapes, including a trial of seven as well</span>
  <span id="freeText13488018983228950124" style="display:none"><i> “Dunk the lunk, thick as a castle wall.” </i><br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed these three novellas. It was great to return to Westeros, one hundred years before the events of ASoIaF. We follow Dunk, a hedge knight risen up by an old knight with no heirs. He gets himself a squire named Egg, who unbeknownst to him is Prince Aegon - one of the Targaryen Princes. <br /><br /><i> “Oak and iron guard me well, or else I’m dead and doomed to hell.” </i><br /><br />We see Dunk get himself into all kinds of scrapes, including a trial of seven as well as numerous other fights. He is a great hero to follow and I loved recognising the names of houses from A Song of Ice and Fire. <br /><br />But what really stood out in this book were the illustrations. They were amazing and really brought the stories and characters to life.<br /><br /> <i> “A head’s a head. They all look the same after a few days on a spike.” </i> <br /><br />With much of the gruesomeness and swearing included in A Song of Ice and Fire; this book helped in my suffering wait for the Winds of Winter. Highly recommend. <br /><br /><i> The summers have been shorter since the last dragon died, and the winters longer and crueler.” </i></span>

<div id="review_1412520536" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1412520536" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1412520536?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1412520536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3541295316901511182">I'm not fond of novellas or short stories. I always end up hating them because of the length. It's like someone telling you a summarized version of a detailed story. This one on the other hand is one of the exceptions to the hatred. It's not a shock though that Martin can make me enjoy something that I typically hate.<br/><br/>This book contains 3 novellas about the adventures of Dunk and Egg. A hedge knight and his squire seeking higher status. Martin is known for his tendency to add in a bunch of plot t</span>
  <span id="freeText3541295316901511182" style="display:none">I'm not fond of novellas or short stories. I always end up hating them because of the length. It's like someone telling you a summarized version of a detailed story. This one on the other hand is one of the exceptions to the hatred. It's not a shock though that Martin can make me enjoy something that I typically hate.<br /><br />This book contains 3 novellas about the adventures of Dunk and Egg. A hedge knight and his squire seeking higher status. Martin is known for his tendency to add in a bunch of plot twists, and the 3 novellas proved no different. The ending was great, because it left me wanting for more and wanting to know who did what. I liked how the unexpected turn of events didn't seem like it was written just for the sake of having a plot twist. <br /><br />The characters were beyond amazing. Dunk and Egg were perfectly written, and developed quite nicely in the end. I can't express how well Martin creates characters. It was most evident in his A Song of Ice and Fire series when I read the first 5 books, but now he proved that he can write amazing new characters. What I enjoyed most about Dunk was that he was a loser. He's not someone who was given everything. He had to work his way to get to the top, and the hardships didn't stop him. I don't hate powerful characters (Like the Starks, for example), but it's refreshing to read about someone who is not of royalty. The journey of a normal boy into a hedge knight was truly entertaining. We all know that being a hedge knight doesn't even result to earning the respect of people. I know that Martin has a few more stories about Dunk and Egg, so hopefully in the future I'd read about Dunk being successful in his journey. Egg was also commendable, but I can't explain how without spoiling. It's better if you find out about the mystery of Egg on your own.<br /><br />The setting is great, but that's a giveaway already if you've read the ASOIAF series. Westeros is truly unforgiving to the weak. It's great to read more about the fictional world that I've loved since A Game of Thrones. This is a minor detour into the main series, in which the sixth book is still unpublished. <br /><br />Do I really need to talk about how great the writing is? <br /><br />4.5/5 stars. If you're unfamiliar with Martin, then you'd better read ASOIAF first. That's just my opinion though, but it did help me enjoy these novellas more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3541295316901511182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1412520536">

<div id="review_2429939791" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2429939791" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2429939791?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2429939791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1686467704694368612">Very entertaining.<br/><br/>George R. R. Martin provides some backstory and depth to his wildly popular Song of Ice and Fire series with this collection of three novellas about Dunc and Egg: a hedge knight and his squire.<br/><br/>The events in the three related and sequential novellas take place a hundred years before <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_' title='A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Game of Thrones</a> and there is still a Targaryen on the iron throne and the memory of the last dragon is still alive in and old man’s memory.<br/><br/>First published all together in 2013, with some snazzy ill</span>
  <span id="freeText1686467704694368612" style="display:none">Very entertaining.<br><br>George R. R. Martin provides some backstory and depth to his wildly popular Song of Ice and Fire series with this collection of three novellas about Dunc and Egg: a hedge knight and his squire.<br><br>The events in the three related and sequential novellas take place a hundred years before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a> and there is still a Targaryen on the iron throne and the memory of the last dragon is still alive in and old man’s memory.<br><br>First published all together in 2013, with some snazzy illustrations by Gary Gianni, Martin gives us a different glimpse into Westeros than what is provided in GOT as we follow these two on some adventures. A hedge knight is similar to a knight errant in our history, a traveling, non-landed swordsman who hires out his services and participates in jousting tournaments. The hedge knight, though a real knight, is of the lowest order and the term itself is somewhat derogatory.<br><br>Our hero, Dunc, naming himself Ser Duncan the Tall – for lack of a better title - was taken from the squalid environs of Fleas Bottom in King’s Landing by a traveling hedge knight and made his squire. Before the old knight dies on the road, he has taught Dunc not just the skills of a squire, but also about chivalry and how to conduct himself as a proper knight should. Dunc’s tutelage seems to have taken hold better than some of the privileged richer classes we meet in the stories. Dunc, maybe not the sharpest tool in the shed, is nonetheless honorable and a very likeable protagonist and for his part trains his squire Egg in the same way.<br><br>The beginning scene, where the old knight has died and Dunc is alone, reminded me of the similar scene in the 2001 Heath Ledger film A Knight’s Tale.<br><br>Not just for GOT fans, this is an enjoyable read for the fantasy crowd.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549209912i/27009917.jpg" width="265" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1686467704694368612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer82832614670229560">If you're into stuff like this, <a href='https://manuelaantao.blogspot.com/2015/12/ser-duncan-tall-knight-of-seven.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>you can read the full review.</a><br/><br/>Ser Duncan the Tall: "A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms" by George R. R. Martin<br/> <br/> <br/>The Knight has three novellas. To wit:<br/> <br/>The Hedge Knight<br/>The Sworn Sword<br/>The Mystery Knight<br/> <br/>I’ve read these three novellas previously when they came out in the three different anthologies: Legends I, Legends II, and Warriors. Having read these stories separately before, I was interested to see them put together as one whole piece, where Martin’s suspicious tende</span>
  <span id="freeText82832614670229560" style="display:none">If you're into stuff like this, <a href="https://manuelaantao.blogspot.com/2015/12/ser-duncan-tall-knight-of-seven.html" rel="nofollow noopener">you can read the full review.</a><br /><br />Ser Duncan the Tall: "A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms" by George R. R. Martin<br /> <br /> <br />The Knight has three novellas. To wit:<br /> <br />The Hedge Knight<br />The Sworn Sword<br />The Mystery Knight<br /> <br />I’ve read these three novellas previously when they came out in the three different anthologies: Legends I, Legends II, and Warriors. Having read these stories separately before, I was interested to see them put together as one whole piece, where Martin’s suspicious tendency for excellent storytelling could flow freely from one chapter to the next, without having to wait for a new novella’s release.<br /> <br />I’m not a big fantasy fan. I have nothing at all against it – it’s just that I enjoy good science fiction more than I enjoy good fantasy. I’ve read and enjoyed Middlearth, The Magician, Tigana, etc. But then came George R.R. Martin. Several people told me to read the first book in his "A Song of Ice and Fire" saga, "A Game of Thrones". I finally succumbed to the thousand-pager, and I'm now hooked, impatiently waiting for Martin to finish the sixth and seventh books in the series to finally read the fifth, "A Dance with Dragons" (it awaits the publication of the "The Winds of Winter" and "A Dream of Spring" to be tackled...).<br /> <br />Read on, if you're into the Ice and Fire Saga.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2159802049" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159802049" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1232712-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552603488p2/1232712.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159802049?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/1232712-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1232712-matt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1232712-matt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159802049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8572950378465208973">I am weak. And in my weakness, I finally broke down and purchased <i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i>. It sat on my shelf for awhile, mocking me and my lack of self-control. I was going to continue ignoring it. But then the seventh season of <i>Game of Thrones</i> came and went, and the withdrawal set in. It set in bad. I had to crack the cover; I had to stop the shakes. <br/><br/>I didn't want to, you see? Really I didn't. <br/><br/>I don’t like encouraging bad behavior. I did not want to be a part – however infinitesimally s</span>
  <span id="freeText8572950378465208973" style="display:none">I am weak. And in my weakness, I finally broke down and purchased <i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i>. It sat on my shelf for awhile, mocking me and my lack of self-control. I was going to continue ignoring it. But then the seventh season of <i>Game of Thrones</i> came and went, and the withdrawal set in. It set in bad. I had to crack the cover; I had to stop the shakes. <br /><br />I didn't want to, you see? Really I didn't. <br /><br />I don’t like encouraging bad behavior. I did not want to be a part – however infinitesimally small – of goading George R.R. Martin into further digressions. I want him to finish <i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i>, a series that I love and that has, in a very real way, broadened my view of the power of books. I never saw myself as the kind of guy who’d liked dragon stories. George cured me of that belief. He made me care. He made me care very, very much.<br /><br />So I read it. And it underwhelmed me. I will leave it up to you whether that was a preordained result. <br /><br /><i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> is a collection of three previously-published novellas concerning Dunk (Ser Duncan the Tall, a seven-foot hedge knight) and Egg (his squire, who is more than he appears). Those novellas are <i>The Hedge Knight</i>, <i>The Sworn Sword</i>, and <i>The Mystery Knight</i>, which take place roughly a century before the events of <i>A Game of Thrones</i>. If you’ve read these before, don’t rush off to get this, since it’s merely an omnibus edition of that material. The stories have been packaged here in chronological order, so that they read pretty seamlessly as a single work. (At 355 pages, it is a very short novel by GRR standards). I should add that <i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> has been lavishly illustrated by Gary Gianni. There is pen-and-ink drawing every few pages. Frankly, this isn’t a thing that strikes my fancy, but I can see how others might appreciate the effort, and recognize some added value. <br /><br />The three stories are of varying quality. In discussing them, I will stick to generalities, in order to avoid spoiling anything (for what it’s worth, I might add). <i>The Hedge Knight</i> is sort of an introduction to Dunk, giving us a bit of his background and character as he attends a tourney at Ashford Meadow. Maybe your mileage will vary, but as I read it, I thought to myself <i>another tourney</i>? After reading about the Tourney of the Hand, and hearing so much about the Great Tourney at Harrenhal, this simply didn't make an impression. This setting has been done, and done much better, elsewhere in the series. <br /><br />The second novella, <i>The Sworn Sword</i>, is dull. It took me awhile to push through it. Dunk and Egg are in Dorne, and get involved in a minor squabble over water between two houses. If riparian rights are your thing, this story will be right in your wheelhouse. I found nothing inherently interesting about it. There wasn’t any good action, any bad sex, or any funny dialogue. Of course, if you like gleaning bits and pieces of mythology – here, there is a lot of talk of the Blackfyre Rebellion – this might be your cup of Dornish red. I’m looking for more. The world-building is awesome in <i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i>, but I don’t want to learn stuff just for the sake of learning stuff (especially stuff that is entirely made-up). I need the world-building to be in the service of a larger storytelling purpose. <br /><br />The final story, <i>The Mystery Knight</i> is actually quite good. It is the one story that broadens the scope, and hints at real stakes. Unsurprisingly, as in many of <i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i>’s best moments, it is set during a wedding. At that, I will say no more. <br /><br />I get that I am a minority opinion when it comes to <i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i>. Part of that might be a touch of bitterness at having had to wait six years (and counting) for the next installment of <i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i> (and the last two installments, <i>A Feast for Crows</i> and <i>A Dance With Dragons</i> have been decidedly average). However, I feel there are some genuine issues with Dunk and Egg that are worth noting. <br /><br />To begin with, Dunk is an uninspired central character. He is tall, he is strong, and as drawn by Gary Gianni, he looks like Fabio. He is also dumb. <i>Dunk the Lunk</i> is the nickname that Dunk has bestowed upon himself. To me, that’s a problem. This is the protagonist we’re talking about. The guy through whose eyes we view the story. He is a dullard, he is slow, he does not say intelligent things, he does not have clear thoughts. He is a plodding bore. That might be fine for a secondary character. But he’s the main attraction. To an extent, his fighting prowess, simplistic code, bullish honor, and single-mindedness recalls the traits of Brienne of Tarth. And to that end, I can stand book-Brienne for only a certain amount of time before getting frustrated. The stories in <i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> don’t allow us to cut away to other viewpoints. We are stuck with the Lunk. <br /><br />(It is not worth comparing the complexities and arcs taken by characters like Jaime, Tyrion, Sansa, or Arya to Ser Duncan the Tall. Dunk does not measure up). <br /><br />Next, we have the writing, which is lazy. I will say that I think GRR is a genius. I will also argue that he has certain unimpeachable literary skills. <i>A Storm of Swords</i> is one of the best books I’ve ever read. Not one of the best <i>fantasy</i> books, but one of the best books, end stop. It will one day reside as a genre-transcending classic. But when we talk about GRR as a great writer, we are not necessarily saying he is a prose stylist. He is an excellent plotter. He creates rich and layered characters. He knows how to execute an unforgettable set-piece, whether that is an unforeseen twist, an unexpected death, or a cinematic battle. <br /><br />GRR also relies on a lot of writerly crutches. He tends to fall back on patterns, motifs, and phrases. You tend not to focus on these during <i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i> because the expansiveness of his canvas dilutes these tics. Here, I couldn’t stop seeing them. For instance, every other thing Dunk says to Egg is a variation of “I’m going to clout your ear.” I don’t know if there was a wager, in which GRR had to use the word “clout” X number of times, but if so, he won. Jeez, Dunk, use another threat already!<br /><br />Finally, the joy of <i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i> is that it is huge. It sprawls. It is like an oil slick, rapidly expanding. There are turns upon twists that are threaded into switchbacks. There are so many details. Details piled atop details. Details all the way down. And the stakes! The stakes are so high. The fate of the world, and all that. <br /><br /><i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i> is indulgent and immersive. It wraps its arms around you in a bear hug and refuses to let you go until you acknowledge that you are living in this world, and that you can no longer tell if it is fiction. <i>How can it be fake when its history goes back so far?</i> You don’t get that feeling with the novellas. The novellas are trifling things. How can upstream water rights or a middling tourney compare to White Walkers? That’s a rhetorical question. <br /><br />While reading <i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i>, I felt an intense need for GRR to finish his opus. Accordingly, here is the part where I gripe. I promise it won’t be lengthy. <br /><br />When fans argue about GRR’s extracurricular activities, the argument often boils down to entitlement. What does George R.R. Martin owe us, as readers? Well, I don’t think he owes me a thing. Likewise, I don’t owe him anything, save maybe the purchase price of his next project. <br /><br />I’ll also admit that if I were GRR, I’d probably be doing the same thing he’s doing, which is enjoying the massive fame he has achieved. I’d be watching football too (though not the Jets). And attending conventions. And earning royalties on everything that has my name. I’d do it all. Well, not the LiveJournal thing. It’s not 2002, after all. But I get it. <br /><br />However, it is a shame. <i>A Song of Ice &amp; Fire</i> is GRR’s masterpiece. It is his legacy. Or will be. When he is gone, it will be the thing that gets etched into his tombstone. As Tywin Lannister would tell him, it’s an accomplishment that will last a thousand years (or at least a century or two). If he completes it, that is. If he does not – it will disappear. No one remembers a story without an ending. <br /><br /><i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> is an <i>amuse-bouche</i>, something to chew on while the main course is finished. I found it hard to enjoy, though, when the completion of that main course is so uncertain.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8572950378465208973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1630269739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630269739" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1630269739?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1630269739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13342445577733907630"><i>"Kings rise and fall, and cows and smallfolk go about their business."</i><br/><br/>I never really planned to read this until I discovered it at the library a few days ago and picked it up. I told myself why not read something short by GRRM for once.<br/>This book is a collection of three novellas, set in the Seven Kingdoms, a century before <i>A Game of Thrones</i>, while the Targaryens are still the ruling House in Westeros.<br/><br/><b>Characters:</b><br/>Dunk, Ser Duncan the Tall, a hedge knight and his squire Egg, Aegon Targaryen (little</span>
  <span id="freeText13342445577733907630" style="display:none"><i>"Kings rise and fall, and cows and smallfolk go about their business."</i><br /><br />I never really planned to read this until I discovered it at the library a few days ago and picked it up. I told myself why not read something short by GRRM for once.<br />This book is a collection of three novellas, set in the Seven Kingdoms, a century before <i>A Game of Thrones</i>, while the Targaryens are still the ruling House in Westeros.<br /><br /><b>Characters:</b><br />Dunk, Ser Duncan the Tall, a hedge knight and his squire Egg, Aegon Targaryen (little brother of Aemon Targaryen, who we know from the Wall in ASOIAF) travel the Seven Kingdoms together. Dunk is a pretty plain character apart from his tallness. It's Egg who actually makes those novellas worth reading.<br /><br /><b>Plot:</b><br />A tournament, a trial, weapons. Lords, lordlings and smallfolk. Dragons, Lions and Stags. Love and death and marriage. A fair maid and a lady. Conspiracy, treason and heads on spikes. Another tournament, another trial and more weapons. And lots of plot twists. It will never once get boring.<br /><br /><b>Writing:</b><br />I can't really say anything about GRRMs writing. It may be smart and witty but never made me emotional. At times it get's repetitive and I could be spared the endless paragraphs about food and drinks and names that I will never remember and never be mentioned again.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to reading more about Dunk and Egg, though I'd prefer to have <i>The Winds of Winter</i> to be honest.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13342445577733907630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1733518710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1733518710" />
    <a title="Poonam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17656456-poonam"><img alt="Poonam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520691179p2/17656456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1733518710?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Poonam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Poonam" href="/user/show/17656456-poonam">Poonam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=group-reads">group-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=paranormal-or-fantasy">paranormal-or-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17656456-poonam?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1733518710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3185267701428051477"><i>This is my Book Of the Month- September 2016, with GR group- Nothing But Reading Challenges- Category: Sci-Fi/Fantasy BOM</i><br/><br/><b>
  <i>"The story offered here takes place about a hundred years prior to the events described in A Game of Thrones"</i>
</b><br/>This was my major concern before picking this up as I have yet to read the Game Of Throne Series (I have watched all the seasons diligently) but still did not want any thing spoiling my enjoyment of reading this series. So you can absolutely pick this up and enjoy t</span>
  <span id="freeText3185267701428051477" style="display:none"><i>This is my Book Of the Month- September 2016, with GR group- Nothing But Reading Challenges- Category: Sci-Fi/Fantasy BOM</i><br><br><b>
  <i>"The story offered here takes place about a hundred years prior to the events described in A Game of Thrones"</i>
</b><br>This was my major concern before picking this up as I have yet to read the Game Of Throne Series (I have watched all the seasons diligently) but still did not want any thing spoiling my enjoyment of reading this series. So you can absolutely pick this up and enjoy the mention of names of all the famous houses that we have come to adore and hate!<br><br>This is a collection of 3 short stories involving Ser Dunkard The Tall i.e. Dunk and Egg (who becomes Dunk's squire). <b>One of the strong points of these stories are the extremely likable protagonists.</b> <br>These stories are available as independent books as well but I would recommend reading these in sequence and together for the maximum enjoyment. This book also has sketches as you read along.<br><br>**Mild Spoilers Ahead**<br><br>The first story is <b>The Hedge Knight</b> where we are first introduced to Dunk and how he comes to meet Egg. Near to the end of the story the true identity of Egg is revealed <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He is none other than Aegon Targaryen <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The concept of Hedge Knight was new to me and I was fascinated with the hierarchy between knights of royal blood, Knights sworn to a lord and hedge knights...<br><br>I absolutely adored Dunk in this story. He was very unsure and always had doubts regarding himself but this made me adore him even more somehow. Some of his innermologues which are repeated throughout the three stories are-<br><b>
  <i>"Dunk the lunk, thought he could be a knight"</i>
</b><br><b>
  <i>"Dunk the lunk, thick as a castle wall."</i>
</b><br><br>There are some very violent moments in this story that made me squirm but by the end of this story I was a True campaigner of Ser Dunkard The Tall.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474029558i/20545126._SY540_.jpg" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The second story -<b>The Sworn Sword</b> takes us further into the journey of Dunk and Egg. In this story it is truly confirmed what a Gallant and Noble knight Dunk truly is- <b>
  <i> "Oak and iron, guard me well, or else I'm dead, and doomed to hell"</i>
</b><br>We come across the Red and Black fight, the effect on the lords and we are introduced to one of the very interesting characters known as the Red Widow.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474031348i/20545452.png" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The last story- <b>The Mystery Knight</b> is the one filled with most twists. There is a competition and a Dragon Egg to be won but that is not the main focus of this story. This is more filled with political intrigue than any of the other stories<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1474032536i/20545613._SY540_.jpg" height="" width="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dunk and Egg are solid together - <b>
  <i>Lord Cockshaw and the Fiddler had brought grooms to tend their horses, cooks to feed them, squires to clean their armor, guards to defend them. Dunk has Egg</i>
</b><br><br>There is also the dreaded Bloodraven who finally makes an appearance <br><b>
  <i>"How many eyes does Lord Bloodraven have? the riddle went. A thousand eyes, and one"</i>
</b> <br><br>I just wanted to read more about Dunk and Egg and hope there are more stories about them.<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3185267701428051477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4385264472351469684"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com'>www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445367747i/16638600._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I just love Dunk & Egg! I just finished reading the two graphic novels of The Hedge Knight and I had no idea this was the book form with a third story of the duo! I just put it on hold at the library because it's George R.R. Martin :) And a friend from GR told me after the fact what it was! <br/><br/>I know there has to be more to it then the graphic novels, but it seems like the book was the same. I loved the first two stories in this book, and the graphic novels. The </span>
  <span id="freeText4385264472351469684" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com">www.melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445367747i/16638600._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I just love Dunk &amp; Egg! I just finished reading the two graphic novels of The Hedge Knight and I had no idea this was the book form with a third story of the duo! I just put it on hold at the library because it's George R.R. Martin :) And a friend from GR told me after the fact what it was! <br><br>I know there has to be more to it then the graphic novels, but it seems like the book was the same. I loved the first two stories in this book, and the graphic novels. The third book is awesome! I really hope to see it in graphic novel soon. <br><br>This third one is called, The Mystery Knight. Dunk and Egg are just going along minding their own business when they meet some Knights on the road. They try to talk them into going to a royal wedding. They don't seem to be who they are and they don't seem trustworthy. Who is? <br><br>Dunk thinks.. well.. maybe he should go and try to win some money for him and Egg so they can be settled nicely for some time. This leads to a big crazy adventure that involves people that are not who they say they are, people getting killed or almost killed, eggs...dragon eggs :) ... more lies and a pretty good ending. <br><br>I had no idea how much I was going to fall in love with Dunk and Egg when I bought the first two graphic novels. Now I just want to read more and more. At the end of the book Mr. Martin says to look forward to more Dunk and Egg travels! Yay! Well, he said it better, but I digress. <br><br>I do want to add this book to my collection at some time and will eagerly await the graphic novel to the third story in this book and many more. Please... many more. <br><br>If you don't like Dunk and Egg, then there is something wrong with you.. so there. Dunk &amp; Egg, sounds like Dunkin Donuts.. I digressed again! Anyhooo.....<br><br>I recommend to ALL George R.R. Martin fans, especially those that love the Game of Thrones as this is years before that time. <div id="review_1813931461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1813931461" />
    <a title="Jason Koivu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu"><img alt="Jason Koivu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560521450p2/1742824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813931461?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813931461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5692348348720111644">This is just what I was looking for! Old timey, good-doer knights and squires doin' good in an old timey setting!<br/><br/>I had picked up a fantasy book a few weeks ago that I hoped would satiate my current reading desires, but alas no. So I turned to George R.R. Martin. He's always a good bet. I like his writing style and I'm familiar with the world he's built. Sure, there's such a small amount of fantasy in his work that, aside from mention of dragons in this particular book, it could almost be called </span>
  <span id="freeText5692348348720111644" style="display:none">This is just what I was looking for! Old timey, good-doer knights and squires doin' good in an old timey setting!<br /><br />I had picked up a fantasy book a few weeks ago that I hoped would satiate my current reading desires, but alas no. So I turned to George R.R. Martin. He's always a good bet. I like his writing style and I'm familiar with the world he's built. Sure, there's such a small amount of fantasy in his work that, aside from mention of dragons in this particular book, it could almost be called historical fiction for its similarity to the York and Tudor War of the Roses back in the 15th century.<br /><br /><i>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms</i> is a collection of three lengthy short stories that follow the adventures of a hedge knight and his squire. Any fan of the Song of Fire &amp; Ice series will recognize many of the names dropped herein even though these stories are set about a hundred years prior. <br /><br />So what you get are some fun action/adventure tales with a helping of Seven Kingdoms history. It's a well-balanced combination. Seldom was I inundated with one or bored with the other. <br /><br />The stakes are high enough to make you care surprisingly deeply about the two main characters by the end of the book. There's good, solid tension through out. And yet, the stakes aren't "Save the World or Bust!!!" high, which is a nice departure from the epic fantasy of the day. <br /><br />In summary, this is a very enjoyable distraction that will entertain the dickens out of Martin's fans!<br /><br /><br />PS: See my videogram book review of this here book by following this here link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ez7U7b7xGRU">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ez7U7...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5692348348720111644" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1522034241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1522034241" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522034241?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007507672" href="/book/show/23306321-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=adventurous-acuity">adventurous-acuity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=anthological-astuteness">anthological-astuteness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522034241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5049151994255592887">George R.R. Martin could write a shopping list and publish it and I would still probably give it five stars!<br/><br/><i> A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms </i> is a collection of three stories set in Westeros, the same fictional lands as featured in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire </i> series, but set over one hundred years previously. This just exemplifies that no-one can world build like Martin can world build! The in-depth knowledge of the land and the familial and ancestral history of the multitude of characters portrayed </span>
  <span id="freeText5049151994255592887" style="display:none">George R.R. Martin could write a shopping list and publish it and I would still probably give it five stars!<br /><br /><i> A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms </i> is a collection of three stories set in Westeros, the same fictional lands as featured in <i>A Song of Ice and Fire </i> series, but set over one hundred years previously. This just exemplifies that no-one can world build like Martin can world build! The in-depth knowledge of the land and the familial and ancestral history of the multitude of characters portrayed is just staggering. This book felt like it had an almost political edge to it on times as it relayed the countless wars, feuds and alliances between the horde of great (and not so great) houses. If you have ever read any Martin before you know that he likes his characters! This book is no different.<br /><br />House Targaryen sits on the throne but we don't view the world from some little lordling's perspective, but from that of a hedge knight. And an admittedly poor one at that. Dunk, or Ser Duncan the Tall, leads us through the world, and it is through his eyes and his experiences that we are introduced to names and places and people that form part of the ancient backstory for <i> A Game of Thrones </i>. That alone was enough to give it five stars, but it was the method used to portray this history that I most liked.<br /><br />The style of narrative was different to what I expected: the reader is offered the limited perspective of only one character, we are distanced from the great houses and given the perspective from one with a lower social standing, and more is withheld from us, allowing us no further knowledge and understanding than what our protagonist can offer us.<br /><br />I found myself liking these aspects. It had a different feel to it than that of its renowned predecessor, giving the book its own separate identity. And yet the same myths and tales still permeated the story. The same places are visited and great names spoken of. The same houses still rule and the same houses still serve. This book doesn't feel new; it feels like coming home.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5049151994255592887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
