    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1405834801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1405834801" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7022024-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470679918p2/7022024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1405834801?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7022024-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7022024-mike?shelf=novella">novella</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1405834801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18171081129107486047">I initially considered holding the fifth star hostage until George R. R. Martin finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12111823.The_Winds_of_Winter__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___6_' title='The Winds of Winter (A Song of Ice and Fire, #6) by George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Winds of Winter</a> but I adored these stories so much I just couldn't do it. <br/><br/>These three novellas take place roughly one hundred years before <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238418235?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Game of Thrones</a>. So all the characters we know and love (and love to hate) have yet to be born, the Targaryens still sit on the Iron Throne, and the small folk are exploited by the nobles (so that much isn't different). Instead of seeing Westeros through the eyes of</span>
  <span id="freeText18171081129107486047" style="display:none">I initially considered holding the fifth star hostage until George R. R. Martin finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12111823.The_Winds_of_Winter__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___6_" title="The Winds of Winter (A Song of Ice and Fire, #6) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winds of Winter</a> but I adored these stories so much I just couldn't do it. <br /><br />These three novellas take place roughly one hundred years before <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238418235?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a>. So all the characters we know and love (and love to hate) have yet to be born, the Targaryens still sit on the Iron Throne, and the small folk are exploited by the nobles (so that much isn't different). Instead of seeing Westeros through the eyes of the Haves (sworn knights, great lords, nobles), we get to see it through the Have-Nots, specifically those of a hedge knight, Ser Duncan the Tall. Unlike the sworn knights who serve a lord, hedge knights travel, seeking service where they can and more often sleeping under hedges than under a roof. Of course don't tell them that.<i>
  <blockquote>"A hedge knight is the truest kind of knight, Dunk," the old man had told him, a long long time ago. "Other knights serve the lords who keep them, or from whom they hold their lands, but we serve where we will, for men whose causes we believe in. Every knight swears to protect the weak and the innocent, but we keep the vow best I think."</blockquote>
</i>I had actually, sort of, already read the first novella, Hedge Knight, in the form of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1178370003?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">the graphic novel</a>. I liked the graphic novel and liked the novella even better. In fact all of the novellas stood very well on their own, not trying to do too much within their story while still doing a fantastic job of developing the relationship between Egg and Dunk. I really liked their relationship and how it grew over the course of the stories.<br /><br />If there is one thing GRRM does well is develop and explain feudal ties and relationships (or maybe he just likes doodling cool house banners). This was very apparent in these stories as Martin does a deft job dropping political developments and themes into the narrative that is ostensibly about the travels of Dunk and Egg. I harbor a suspicion that the entire purpose of the Song of Ice and Fire series is to show how terrible monarchies and aristocracies are.<br /><br />In this case Dunk and Egg are confronted on several occasions by the fall out from the <a href="http://awoiaf.westeros.org/index.php/First_Blackfyre_Rebellion" rel="nofollow noopener">Blackfyre Rebellion</a>*. The nickel tour is this: The Blackfyre Rebellion was a civil war in Westeros over who should succeed to the Iron Throne (<i>Some old dead king gave a sword to one son instead of another, that was the start of it. And now I'm standing here, and poor Roger's in his grave.</i>). The realm was split, one side (the Blackfyres) lost and several members of that family fled Westeros, looming as a threat to the victorious side. As with all civil wars, one group ends up backing the wrong side and faces the consequences, most notably losing land, titles, holdings, respect of the victors, and being forced to provide hostages to the victor's side. But just because there was a winner doesn't mean the losers were content to just go back to the status quo ante. All that politics aside, even though the rebellion occurred fifteen years prior to the events of these novellas the repercussions still echo throughout the realm.<i>
  <blockquote>"Treason... is only a word. When two princes fight for a chair where only one may sit, great lords and common man alike must choose. and when the battle's done, the victors will be hailed as loyal men and true, whilst those who were defeated will be known forevermore as rebels and traitors."</blockquote>
</i>So as Dunk and Egg (his squire) travel about they are confronted with these consequences: lords who backed the wrong (though not in their mind) side, conspirators to return the Blackfyres, political discontent with the current regime who many believe is being controlled by a sorcerer bastard offspring of the previous king.<br /><br />There is a great balance of fights, character development, narrative progression, and political intrigue. I got a much better view on the lives of the small folk and lesser knights (not surprisingly: just as sucky as I previously assumed) as well as the challenges that the vast majority of Westeros must deal with, small folk and petty noble alike. Heck, one novella revolves around water rights between two nobles of a stream during a drought (and we also see one of the many repercussions of the Blackfyre Rebellion). <br /><br />But the heart of these books is the relationship between Dunk (Ser Duncan the Tall) and Egg (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(don't open this unless you really want to know) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ (I'm serious, it is sort of the big reveal of the first novella) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a href="http://awoiaf.westeros.org/index.php/Aegon_V_Targaryen" rel="nofollow noopener">Aegon Targaryen V</a> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>).<blockquote>
  <i>"Can I have a sword to run them off with?"<br />"No. A knife's enough. And you had best be here when I come back, do you hear me? Rob me and run off, and I'll hunt you down, I swear I will. With dogs."<br />"You don't have any dogs."<br />"I'll get some, just for you."</i>
</blockquote>OK, so they don't start off on the best of terms, but once they settle into the knight-squire relationship they develop respect and admiration for each other.<blockquote>
  <i>"Pour Ser Duncan a cup of sweet Dornish Red [Egg]. Try not to spill it on him, you've done him sufficient ill already."<br />"The boy won't spill, Your Grace. He's a good boy. A good squire. And he meant no harm to me, I know."<br />"One need not intend harm to do it."<br /><br />~~~<br /><br />"Well, some knights sing gallant songs to their ladies, or play them tunes upon a lute."<br />"I have no lute. And that night I drank too much in the Planky Town, you told me I sang like an ox in mud in a mud wallow."<br />"I had forgotten, ser."<br />"How could you forget?"<br />"You told me to forget, ser. You told me I'd get a clout in the ear the next time I mentioned it."<br /><br />~~~<br /><br />"Ser? That fat septon said my father sulks in Summerhall."<br />"Words are wind."<br />"My father doesn't sulk."<br />"Well, he might. <b>You</b> sulk."<br />"I do not. Ser. Do I?"<br />"Some. Not too often, though. Elsewise I'd clout you in the ear more than I do."<br />"You clouted me in the ear at the gate."<br />"That was half a clout at best. If I ever give you a whole clout, you'll know."</i>
</blockquote>And while Dunk pretty consistently threatens to clout Egg, it rarely happens, it is more a playful type of threat. Dunk clearly treats Egg with all the respect due a squire without abusing his power over him. Egg is stronger in some matters and instead of resenting Egg for it, Dunk makes use of it. All in all a great relationship that I enjoyed to see blossom. Even though GRRM is way behind on Winds of Winter, I really hope we end up with more Dunk and Egg stories.<br /><br />And now for some great passages:<br /><br /><b>Wisdom even in the real world</b>: <i><br />A peasant's pride is a lordling's shame.<br />~<br />Kings rise and fall and cows and smallfolk go about their business<br />~<br />"Some rebel lord or robber knight, it was. Or maybe a common murderer. A head's a head. they all look the same after a few days on spike."</i><br /><br /><b>Maybe GRRM has moonlight as a porn writer</b>: <i>The sun rose hot and hard, implacable.</i><br /><br /><b>Egg, master fighting strategists</b>: <i>"Get him, ser," he heard Egg call. "Get him, get him, he's right there."</i><br /><br /><b>The only time anyone was glad an Ironborn was nearby</b>: <i>"Count yourself fortunate that I am ironborn. The priests of the Drowned God know how to drown a man and bring him back, and I have made a study of their beliefs and customs."</i><br /><br /><b>Even fleas have standards</b>: <i>"We won't have any [money] if we start sleeping in inns. You want to share a bed with some peddler and wake up with his fleas? Not me. I have my own fleas, and they are not fond of strangers. We'll sleep beneath the stars."</i><br /><br />*If you want to learn more about the history of Westeros I cannot recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1149926018?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The World of Ice and Fire</a> enough. Great history and amazing pictures.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18171081129107486047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2094017289" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2094017289" />
    <a title="Sud666" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666"><img alt="Sud666" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418437112p2/36890366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2094017289?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sud666" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sud666" href="/user/show/36890366-sud666">Sud666</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36890366-sud666?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2094017289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18078496845049153974">I have read the comic version of this but I ran across a particularly nice illustrated copy and bought it. I am glad I did. This is a very entertaining tale. It is slightly more light hearted in overall tone, but don't let good ol' Dunk and adorable Egg fool you-this is still the world of Game of Thrones. NOTHING is what it seems. There is violence and maiming a plenty.<br/><br/>One Hundred years before the events of the Game of Thrones timeline there was a hedge knight named Ser Duncan. Ser Duncan finds </span>
  <span id="freeText18078496845049153974" style="display:none">I have read the comic version of this but I ran across a particularly nice illustrated copy and bought it. I am glad I did. This is a very entertaining tale. It is slightly more light hearted in overall tone, but don't let good ol' Dunk and adorable Egg fool you-this is still the world of Game of Thrones. NOTHING is what it seems. There is violence and maiming a plenty.<br /><br />One Hundred years before the events of the Game of Thrones timeline there was a hedge knight named Ser Duncan. Ser Duncan finds a young bald boy named Egg and makes him his squire. So begins their journey to make a name for themselves. Along the way they run into Lords, Princes and many other famous houses from the GOT story. Just 100 years before. That snot nosed boy being bounced on Lord Frey's lap? Mostly likely the old, dying Lord Frey of the GOT timeline. But you will recognize some of the famous names.<br /><br />Broken into three short novellas it shows Ser Duncan the Tall and his adventures in a tournament held by Lord Ashford- this is really the origin story of Ser Duncan the Tall. You also find out about Egg.<br />The second story is a little after those events and it's a very good one. I enjoyed it because it shows the complexity of being a minor noble house in these times. The aspect of honor really is important in this story and it shows what kind of knight Ser Duncan is.<br />The Third story can really be called the Second Blackfyre Rebellion. If that means nothing to you then good-you'll learn all about the First one in this short story. You will also find out how Ser Duncan and Egg were able to foil a plot to overthrow the King.<br /><br />All of the stories were written with the GRR Martin flare and are quite enjoyable. The artists Gary Gianni is to be lauded. I loved his artwork. I wish they could have been in color but the black and white illustration are great representations of the events and they are plentiful-I loved that! A great book for any GOT fan. A great book for someone who has no idea what GOT is-this might make you one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18078496845049153974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1394675913" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394675913" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1394675913?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=arc-review">arc-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394675913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2359013269795903672">I love a great narrator for an audiobook, especially one that can not only do all the different voices, but act the parts. Harry Lloyd does a splendid job with these novellas, he acts so perfectly, giving weight to the simplest phrase. I was extremely impressed.<br/><br/>Having said that (I hear the collective groan), there's one problem I find with these incredible actor/narrators: <br/><br/> Sometimes they actually whisper when the scene calls for whispering. <br/><br/>I hate it. I have my audiobook going, I'm either in th</span>
  <span id="freeText2359013269795903672" style="display:none">I love a great narrator for an audiobook, especially one that can not only do all the different voices, but act the parts. Harry Lloyd does a splendid job with these novellas, he acts so perfectly, giving weight to the simplest phrase. I was extremely impressed.<br /><br />Having said that (I hear the collective groan), there's one problem I find with these incredible actor/narrators: <br /><br /> Sometimes they actually whisper when the scene calls for whispering. <br /><br />I hate it. I have my audiobook going, I'm either in the car on my way to work or have the ear buds in doing the dishes. My hands are busy driving or soapy from cleaning. I don't have the ability nor patience to rewind (you can still say rewind right?) the recording back to listen to the part I just missed because the narrator whispered the line instead of stage-whispered the line so I could hear it with the same volume I had for normal talking.<br /><br />It's a pet-peeve of mine and typically on find it happens with the best of narrators. Catch-22 I guess. (This review lost no stars for review author's pet-peeves)<br /><br />Thanks for letting me get that out of my system. On to some substance.<br /><br />A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms is the collection of Dunk and Egg novellas found in various anthologies (Legends, Legends II, and Warriors), all of which I already owned in print and the first of which I'd already read in print.<br /><br />These novellas are the perfect way to get back to the Seven Kingdoms when you feel yourself missing them. They don't require a knowledge of the rest of the series, A Song of Ice and Fire, but it doesn't hurt to have that knowledge either. It has the same feel, if a bit lighter and more fun in a buddy-cop (buddy-knight?) sort of way.<br /><br />The Hedge Knight is probably my favorite of the bunch. It's the introduction to the characters, has a great jousting tournament, and all kinds of surprises to keep you going.<br /><br />The Sworn Sword is almost as good and deals with our heroes swearing themselves to a minor Lord (hence sworn sword of course). They have an issue with water law, which I found to be great having taken a water law course in law school and practiced some as well through an internship. Riparian rights people! If only it were so simple. It's not.<br /><br />Finally, there's The Mystery Knight, which starts out as another simple jousting tournament, but turns everything on its head. The weakest of the bunch, but for George RR Martin, that still means it's better than most things.<br /><br />In sum, Dunk and Egg stories are perfect when you're needing your Game of Thrones fix, even better if you don't want to leave completely depressed, and in a note at the end of this collection, George reveals there are plenty more adventures throughout the Seven Kingdoms and beyond. I can't wait!<br /><br />4.5 out of 5 Stars (very highly recommended)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2359013269795903672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1459686576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1459686576" />
    <a title="Shivam Chaturvedi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42731007-shivam-chaturvedi"><img alt="Shivam Chaturvedi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565684213p2/42731007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1459686576?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shivam Chaturvedi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shivam Chaturvedi" href="/user/show/42731007-shivam-chaturvedi">Shivam Chaturvedi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007507672" href="/book/show/23306321-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42731007-shivam-chaturvedi?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42731007-shivam-chaturvedi?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42731007-shivam-chaturvedi?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42731007-shivam-chaturvedi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1459686576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3469928355913029504">This book is a collection of three stories involving two immensely likeable protagonists named Dunk and Egg. Delightfully illustrated in black and white, it follows their travels through the length and breadth of the <i>Seven Kingdoms</i>, about ninety years prior to the events in <i>A Game of Thrones</i>. Dunk, or <b>Ser Duncan the Tall</b>, is an ordinary run of the mill hedge knight who will one day be Lord Commander of the Kingsguard. Egg, or <b>Aegon Targaryen</b>, is the fourth son of the fourth son of Daeron II Targ</span>
  <span id="freeText3469928355913029504" style="display:none">This book is a collection of three stories involving two immensely likeable protagonists named Dunk and Egg. Delightfully illustrated in black and white, it follows their travels through the length and breadth of the <i>Seven Kingdoms</i>, about ninety years prior to the events in <i>A Game of Thrones</i>. Dunk, or <b>Ser Duncan the Tall</b>, is an ordinary run of the mill hedge knight who will one day be Lord Commander of the Kingsguard. Egg, or <b>Aegon Targaryen</b>, is the fourth son of the fourth son of Daeron II Targaryen, King of Westeros in 209 AC. Egg, as Aegon V, will himself one day be King and be known as <i>Aegon the Unlikely</i> for having been the lowest in the line of succession. Our heroes don't know it yet, ofcourse. These are their formative years, when a series of unlikely events will lead to a prince squiring for an ordinary hedge knight and how the two will shape, transform and help each other.<br><br>The three stories in themselves aren't overtly spectacular, but Martin's characteristic storytelling and the vivid feeling of a more chivalrous, <i>medieval</i> setting (since we usually associate Song of Ice and Fire with the present, so to speak) gives the tales their charming flavor. The fact that Ser Duncan is the POV character of these stories makes them all the more relatable for we are no longer seeing the world of Westeros from the eyes of great lords and ladies but from those of a commoner. The dreams and aspirations of a simpleton ring truer and contrast sharply with those eyeing the Iron Throne a hundred years later.<br><br>The shadow of the first <i>Blackfyre Rebellion</i> hangs low like a cloud over Westeros in these stories. The events of this rebellion are slated to have taken place a little over a decade ago, when the current King Daeron was challenged by his bastard brother <b>Daemon Blackfyre</b> for the Iron Throne. As an aside to the three tales, the rebellion itself makes for a much interesting side story, adding depth and realism to this fantasy universe. And as is true for every story, the stories of the Blackfyre rebellion throw up yet another remarkable cast of characters, a credit to the brilliance of George RR Martin. The questions regarding the nature of loyalty and treason are often brought up in reference to this event and lead to several interesting dialogues between the different characters.<br><br><b>The Tales of Dunk and Egg, #1-3</b><br><br><b>1) The Hedge Knight</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454571459i/17982561.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Dunk and Egg travel to the town of Ashford in the <i>Reach</i> to participate in a tourney being hosted there. Dunk hopes to gain a few victories which will set him up well to become a proper knight. His chance encounter with the runaway prince Aegon, Egg, leads to the latter squiring for him without the prior's knowledge. Harmless as it may seem, Dunk doesn't know the turn events will soon take, changing not only his, but the fate of the great Targaryen dynasty.<br><br><b>2) The Sworn Sword</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454669153i/17996824.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Following on from the Ashford tourney, Dunk and Egg enter into the service of a little known Lord Eustance Osgrey of Standfast and help him against the maneuvers of the <i>Red Widow</i>, lady of a rival house in times of a great drought across the Reach. As is usual though with Martin's stories, all may not be as simple as it seems. <br><br><b>3) The Mystery Knight</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454669153i/17996825._SY540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Dunk and Egg are on their way to Winterfell to take service with the Starks, who are fighting off with the Greyjoys. On their way north, they encounter a travelling party on its way to a wedding and tourney in the <i>Riverlands</i>. Eager to make some money before their hard journey north, our duo fall along with the party, completely unaware that the wedding/tourney is only a pretext for the Blackfyre sympathizers to meet and plan the second rebellion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3469928355913029504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1411369865" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1411369865" />
    <a title="Marquise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4674014-marquise"><img alt="Marquise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445405166p2/4674014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1411369865?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marquise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marquise" href="/user/show/4674014-marquise">Marquise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4674014-marquise?shelf=here-be-valiant-knights">here-be-valiant-knights</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4674014-marquise?shelf=best-loved-reads">best-loved-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4674014-marquise?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4674014-marquise?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1411369865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10696855581146856892">This isn't a new series of novellas but rather a collection of the three existing books featuring Ser Duncan the Tall, a hugely clumsy and hugely lovable seventeen-year-old hedge knight...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444404236i/16496631._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>... and his sharp-tongued little squire, Prince Aegon of House Targaryen, nicknamed Egg for obvious reasons (look at his name, and then look at his bald head):<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444404236i/16496632._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The stories themselves are old favourites in the ASOIAF fandom, no need to describe or review them, and besides we all know everyone bought this edition </span>
  <span id="freeText10696855581146856892" style="display:none">This isn't a new series of novellas but rather a collection of the three existing books featuring Ser Duncan the Tall, a hugely clumsy and hugely lovable seventeen-year-old hedge knight...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444404236i/16496631._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>... and his sharp-tongued little squire, Prince Aegon of House Targaryen, nicknamed Egg for obvious reasons (look at his name, and then look at his bald head):<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444404236i/16496632._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The stories themselves are old favourites in the ASOIAF fandom, no need to describe or review them, and besides we all know everyone bought this edition because of the art by Gary Gianni. It's known!<br><br>Mr Gianni, who also did the 2014 A Song of Ice and Fire calendar with a dozen choice scenes from the books, here has produced a grand total of 160 illustrations, all in black and white inking, some quite simple and minimalistic and others so detailed and intricate, in a beautiful style that calls to memory the old-school chivalry graphic novel "Prince Valiant" by artist Hal Foster, which is surely not a coincidence as Gary Gianni undertook the continuation of the franchise after Foster's death, though coloured and not inked as the story used to be in the beginning. And Martin is a fan as well. I am very pleased with this resemblance, because I am a fan of "Prince Valiant" myself, and the tone of that story is quite fitting for Duncan, one of the few <i>true knights</i> that Martin has created (and miraculously not killed . . . yet).<br><br>The best illustrations are, unsurprisingly, for the first story, entitled "The Hedge Knight," which is also the one that has the higher number of drawings. It's also my favourite of the novellas, and it was a pleasure to see all the iconic scenes illustrated. Speaking of iconic scenes, Gianni didn't overlook even the naked huntress dream Dunk has! Fans will remember what I mean. That one, the second novella "The Sworn Sword" is the one that has the more intimate illustrations, and the third one, "The Mystery Knight," has the next best illustrations after the first novella, in my opinion.<br><br>Some of the artist's interpretations were disappointing, which was to be expected since there are some scenes that were different for me in my head, such as the scenes with the Fiddler. And other small details were a surprise, such as Ser Duncan's appearance, in particular I found his nose was strangely button-like, that might be a matter of style in truth (and Prince Valiant had the same kind of nose, I seem to recall) and it gives him an air of innocent youth at odds with his big-boned 7 foot body. I had a bigger issue with the depiction of Tanselle Too-Tall, who in Gianni's interpretation doesn't seem tall <i>at all</i>, and that was grating because . . . there's a reason for why she has the moniker Too-Tall and her height is plot-relevant.<br><br>This is a book for fantasy fans and chivalry-epic lovers to have, both for the stories and the great art.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10696855581146856892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5774104705278866801" style="display:none">'A century before A GAME OF THRONES, two unlikely heroes wandered Westeros.'<br /><br />A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms book is a prequel story of A Song of Ice and Fire.<br /> <br />This book contains three novels:<br />The Hedge Knight<br />The Sworn Sword<br />The Mystery Knight<br /><br />A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms book is more for the young readers.             Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=contains-romance">contains-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=epics">epics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=war">war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77983193-zitong-ren?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3073314410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15536364443847233947">4.5🌟<br/><br/>Ahh, yes, Martin. The author that seems to take forever to write a book, yet I can’t help but love everyone all of his fantasy books. I, like many other fantasy readers out there, have been waiting on the Winds of a Winter for a while now(though since I only read A Song of Ice and Fire last year, the wait has not been nearly as long as for some other people), and decided to venture back into the land of Westeros. After finishing this book, I did not realise how much I needed to be back into </span>
  <span id="freeText15536364443847233947" style="display:none">4.5🌟<br /><br />Ahh, yes, Martin. The author that seems to take forever to write a book, yet I can’t help but love everyone all of his fantasy books. I, like many other fantasy readers out there, have been waiting on the Winds of a Winter for a while now(though since I only read A Song of Ice and Fire last year, the wait has not been nearly as long as for some other people), and decided to venture back into the land of Westeros. After finishing this book, I did not realise how much I needed to be back into his world, which really surprised me as I did not think it would bring back so many memories of when I first read the main series.<br /><br />It is a set of short stories, a trilogy if you can call it that, that follows a Hedge Knight and his squire about a century before the events of the main series. The thing I find to be fascinating about this book, and this series in general, is that, there is a real lack of fantastical elements and due to the grittiness of it all, it makes it feel almost like it is more of a medieval setting rather than a fantastical setting maybe apart from the few mentions of dragons.<br /><br />One thing I do think that Martin triumphs on, compared to many other authors is his ability to set the political scene and really show the world for what it is, full of betrayals, schemes and people killing each other behind each other’s backs. That, I think, is what makes A Song of Ice and Fire great. It makes it feel much more real and now that I am used to his prose, the story actually flows so well and makes it so easy to read which is like, wow, this is good.<br /><br />The characters are brilliant and the setting, as I have mentioned, is phenomenal. There are so many lords, ladies and knights that makes the world feel full and whole, instead of empty, as I have called out some fantasy books to be. The world is always full of stuff, good and bad, so why shouldn’t fantasy book or world be?<br /><br />It’s a surprisingly short read, and added with all of the pictures, it is not on the level of epicness or scope of the main series, but for what it is, I really loved it to bits. It’s not long, and if you do need something to make you feel fulfilled whilst waiting for the Winds of Winter(if it ever comes out), than I highly do recommend this book. I do also recommend that the main series be read first as there are many elements, names and themes that a first time reader of the world of Westeros would not understand. 9/10</span>

<div id="review_2068622025" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2068622025?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie | ab_reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie | ab_reads" href="/user/show/53055819-abbie-ab-reads">Abbie | ab_reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007507672" href="/book/show/23306321-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2068622025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2697362170400214353">If you're tired of waiting for Winds of Winter to come out before you die and you haven't already picked up A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms, then I urge you to do so! I had SO MUCH FUN gallivanting around the Seven Kingdoms with Dunk and Egg, it was amazing to be immersed back into GRRM's epic high fantasy world.<br/>.<br/>I absolutely adore ASOIAF, but even I realise that sometimes GRRM can ramble on a bit, especially during the big history dumps. This book is made up of three separate adventures though, </span>
  <span id="freeText2697362170400214353" style="display:none">If you're tired of waiting for Winds of Winter to come out before you die and you haven't already picked up A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms, then I urge you to do so! I had SO MUCH FUN gallivanting around the Seven Kingdoms with Dunk and Egg, it was amazing to be immersed back into GRRM's epic high fantasy world.<br />.<br />I absolutely adore ASOIAF, but even I realise that sometimes GRRM can ramble on a bit, especially during the big history dumps. This book is made up of three separate adventures though, and is therefore snappier! The action and antics never stop, and the illustrations made it even more fun. There are seriously illustrations on almost every other page to really help you visualise Dunk and Egg's adventures if Martin's rich prose isn't quite enough! I loved all three of the sequences, but I think my fave was the second one, as I just loved Lady Rohanne!<br />.<br />It was also great to read a book set in the time of Targaryen rule; there are hints all through ASOIAF of their bad/mad/sad kings and princes, and we finally get to see some of them in action! I got confused by a lot of the names, but what's new there? There was no shortage of back-stabbing knights, lordly feuds, rebellion, all jam-packed into this volume!<br />.<br />Definitely recommend this gem! The only thing I'd complain about was that none of our faves are there... but I knew this going in, it's set 100 years in the past so I am not allowed to complain that the Hound's not there calling everyone a c**t haha!<br />.</span>

<div id="review_2303938214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2303938214" />
    <a title="leynes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes"><img alt="leynes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593512704p2/45198798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2303938214?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="leynes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="leynes" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes">leynes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780007507672" href="/book/show/23306321-a-knight-of-the-seven-kingdoms">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303938214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9588978503935599952">Imagine being a kid again, impatiently waiting for your birthday. Then, when the day finally comes around, you wake up to realize that someone has swapped all of your gifts and you’re literally left with a box full of shit. That’s how I am feeling right now.<br/><br/>Okay, that's maybe a tad bit overdramatic but I have been hyped for these novellas for a long time. I am veeeerry invested into the world of ice and fire, and learning about the history of Westeros and all the shit that paved the way for the </span>
  <span id="freeText9588978503935599952" style="display:none">Imagine being a kid again, impatiently waiting for your birthday. Then, when the day finally comes around, you wake up to realize that someone has swapped all of your gifts and you’re literally left with a box full of shit. That’s how I am feeling right now.<br /><br />Okay, that's maybe a tad bit overdramatic but I have been hyped for these novellas for a long time. I am veeeerry invested into the world of ice and fire, and learning about the history of Westeros and all the shit that paved the way for the mess we’re currently in is totally my thing, so this should’ve worked. However, good ole George decided to bless me with sentences like this:<blockquote>
  <b>Across her small breasts was a faint spray of freckles, and her nipples were red and hard as little berries. <br /><br />His bladder had been full to bursting. The piss went on and on. <br /><br />Dunk’s piss began to flow again. He gave his cock a shake, and laced himself back up.</b>
</blockquote>Bit of an overshare, huh? George’s fascination with nipples and body fluids is something that I will never understand, but I am not one to kinkshame. ;) Just overall, these novellas irritated the shit out of me. <br /><br />I loved Egg (with all of my heart) and hated Dunk (with a passion). Egg was awesome since he provided all of the comic relief in the story, was overall just adorable and pure, and his loyalty had me shook. Honestly, I would read the shit out of a series with him as a POV character. He was clever, witty, and the one who kept me invested in the series. <br /><br />Dunk, however, just pissed me off. His character seemed what I imagine that one dude from Guardians of the Galaxy to be—a bit of a teddy bear type of character who is awkward around women but then super strong and somewhat clumsy and weird, but saves the day… and ugh, I just hated him tbh. Especially his interactions with all of the female characters and his awkward fixation on their bodies just made me highkey uncomfortable (especially their nipples, but we covered that already). <br /><br />Also, Egg was always such a loyal hoe and really cared for Dunk and was scared for him and wanted to protect him, but when Dunk thought that Egg was dead we almost got no reaction from him?? Like for real, such a punk ass motherfucker… Egg deserves better. ;)<blockquote>
  <b>How many eyes does Lord Bloodraven have? A thousand eyes, and one.</b>
</blockquote>Apart from the characters, the plot left me quite underwhelmed as well. <i>The Hedge Knight</i> takes place in 209 AC, some 90 years before the events in ASOIAF, and tells how Egg became Dunk’s squire, and everything that went down at the tournament at Ashford Meadow—the famous tourney during which Prince Baelor Targaryen (the Prince of Dragonstone, son and heir of King Daeron II Targaryen, and Hand of the King) was accidentally killed by his own brother. <br /><br /><i>The Sworn Sword</i> focuses on the difficult path of chivalry when taking part in petty feuds and casual injustices are part and parcel of what it means to be a sworn man in the feudal Seven Kingdoms. <br /><br /><i>The Mystery Knight</i> details the second Blackfyre Rebellion—the failed plot which took place in 211 AC at Whitewalls, where the hedge knight known as Ser John the Fiddler was revealed to be Daemon II Blackfyre during a wedding tourney, and taken captive by Lord Bloodraven (the later Three Eyed Crow). <br /><br />So sure, some interesting shit happened that helped me map out Westeros’ history even better in my mind, and also made me wonder HOW OLD AEMON FUCKING TARGARYEN IS??? LIKE FOR REAL HOW WAS HE STILL ALIVE AND STRIVING WHEN JON CAME TO THE WALL. HOW???<br /><br />Anyways, but apart from some little neat information, the plot really didn’t offer anything good. It dragged like a bitch (to put it in George’s own words) and wasn’t all that exciting. The repetition of shitty phrases (dunk, the lunk, sick as a castle wall etc.) just made me aggressive and made me want to throw the book across the room. Argh. <br /><br />In conclusion, I am left disappointed. "It makes no difference. That was what you were supposed to say, though it made all the difference in the world."—probably, the only thing me and Dunk can agree on. This really shouldn’t be a big deal but I can’t help but feel thoroughly disappointed and unsatisfied.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9588978503935599952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1416400110" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1416400110" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1416400110?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1416400110" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16144911595857217471">I wanted to read this slooooooowly so I'd have more of GRRM's fantastic world to read about until <b>Winds of Winter</b> hits the shelves but I just couldn't stop myself. This isn't just a book to make further money with. I mean, it certainly was aimed to make further money, but the stories are solid, the world-building as fantastic as in the full-length novels and the characters as vivid as ever. The author is giving his readers some real treats so yeah, he can have my money!<br/>Rounding off the three nov</span>
  <span id="freeText16144911595857217471" style="display:none">I wanted to read this slooooooowly so I'd have more of GRRM's fantastic world to read about until <b>Winds of Winter</b> hits the shelves but I just couldn't stop myself. This isn't just a book to make further money with. I mean, it certainly was aimed to make further money, but the stories are solid, the world-building as fantastic as in the full-length novels and the characters as vivid as ever. The author is giving his readers some real treats so yeah, he can have my money!<br>Rounding off the three novellas about Ser Duncan the Tall and his squire Egg is some quite enchanting artwork (160 illustrations to be exact) by a very talented Gary Gianni.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445200165i/16613944._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>About the stories:<br>GRRM has written 4 novellas about the World of <i>A Song Of Ice And Fire</i> so far. The first three are called <i>The Hedge Knight</i>, <i>The Sworn Sword</i>, and <i>The Mystery Knight</i>. They are all about a Hedge Knight, who was born in the notorious Flea Bottom in King's Landing, called Ser Duncan the Tall<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445200341i/16613968._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445200165i/16613945._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and his squire who is (no spoiler here) the crown-prince Aegon V Targaryen ("Egg").<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445200165i/16613946._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Egg, by the way (for those who need a reminder) is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maester Aemon's brother he was hallucinating about shortly before he died. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The adventures as experienced by this unlikely duo happened about a century before the story in <b>A Game of Thrones</b> begins. So it can be seen as a prequel. You don't have to know these stories in order to understand the novels but for fans like me it was a wonderful opportunity to dive into the world once more.<br><br>I'm glad the original plan to publish these stories in anthologies could not be realized because the stories were too long. And it was very nice of GRRM to say that those readers who already bought the novellas in anthologies should get more than just the same stories again so we all got these beautiful illustrations. I much prefer a book with GRRM's stories alone and hope that his other novella, <b>The Princess and the Queen</b> about the Dance of the Dragons will be published again in an exclusive volume too (mabe he'll even write some more stories to put in that second book?).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445200165i/16613947._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36873041-amanda-never-mandy?shelf=g-o-t-death">g-o-t-death</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1412338717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10714185302460324387">The last GOT I read was a bit long and a bit dry. It wasn’t even my idea to buy this one, that’s how much I didn’t anticipate the boredom. I just happen to live with a collector that has to own all the books in a series and I am unable to refuse a crisp new book showing up on my doorstep. <br/><br/>Mmm…that new book smell.<br/><br/>Lucky me, this was outstanding! I can honestly say I enjoyed it more than the rest of the series. I instantly fell in love with the two main characters and was on the edge of my seat ant</span>
  <span id="freeText10714185302460324387" style="display:none">The last GOT I read was a bit long and a bit dry. It wasn’t even my idea to buy this one, that’s how much I didn’t anticipate the boredom. I just happen to live with a collector that has to own all the books in a series and I am unable to refuse a crisp new book showing up on my doorstep. <br /><br />Mmm…that new book smell.<br /><br />Lucky me, this was outstanding! I can honestly say I enjoyed it more than the rest of the series. I instantly fell in love with the two main characters and was on the edge of my seat anticipating each and every moment. Dunk is just perfection in my eyes and the author’s writing style blew me away with how it painted a mental picture of him. Don't get me started on the artwork, it was phenomenal!! Not too much to distract, but just enough to compliment.<br /><br />Story one by far was my favorite and story two was what I expected of a middle story, just a transitional and/or character growing experience. Story three worked well as a finisher, well at least for this fragment of the big picture. With the author’s latest delay news (no surprise), I will no longer anticipate any kind of future with his writing in regards to this series. The show obviously takes precedence and I don’t have a taste for it.<br /><br />**NOTE: I realize this book technically isn't in the GOT series and that it occurs in the same world, just so many years prior. In my reading universe they do connect; therefore I like referring to them as a "series" or collecting them that way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10714185302460324387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1055914915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1055914915" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9595345-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362241942p2/9595345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1055914915?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/9595345-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9595345-lisa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1055914915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16214481677208739623">Review originally posted at The Speculative Herald: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.speculativeherald.com/2015/10/26/review-a-knight-of-seven-kingdoms-by-george-r-r-martin/'>http://www.speculativeherald.com/2015...</a><br/><br/>A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms is a compilation of the first three Dunk and Egg short stories by George R. R. Martin that have previously been available in separate anthologies. I have been wanting to read these for years, and have just not hunted down copies of the separate anthologies yet. Now that they are conveniently packaged together, I figured there was no excuse. And as an added bonus, the art wor</span>
  <span id="freeText16214481677208739623" style="display:none">Review originally posted at The Speculative Herald: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.speculativeherald.com/2015/10/26/review-a-knight-of-seven-kingdoms-by-george-r-r-martin/">http://www.speculativeherald.com/2015...</a><br /><br />A Knight of the Seven Kingdoms is a compilation of the first three Dunk and Egg short stories by George R. R. Martin that have previously been available in separate anthologies. I have been wanting to read these for years, and have just not hunted down copies of the separate anthologies yet. Now that they are conveniently packaged together, I figured there was no excuse. And as an added bonus, the art work in it makes getting the physical copy of the book well worth it.<br /><br />A Knight of Seven Kingdoms tells three tales in the traveling adventures of Dunk and Egg. The first story, The Hedge Knight introduces us to both Dunk and Egg, as well as how they met and some their history prior to being brought together. We also learn about the life of a hedge knight. It was a fun story, and I quickly latched on to both Dunk and Egg. The second story and third stories each highlight a particular escapade in their travels. They are interesting and engaging, and Dunk and Egg are characters I want to read more about. Especially Egg (and Dunk)!<br /><br />I found these stories to be really fun and much lighter than A Song of Ice and Fire. We know Martin can create excellent dynamics between duos from Arya and the Hound, Brienne and Jaime, Tyrion and Bronn. Well, Tyrion and pretty much anyone. Set hundreds of years before A Song of Ice and Fire, these short stories center on another duo, Dunk and Egg. The stories honestly just left me feeling good. I mean I absolutely love ASoIaF, but in general it doesn’t leave me feeling like this. Perhaps the sections with Arya and Hound, and maybe some other sections, but the overall tone of ASoIaF is much graver and tense. The wonderful thing about these short stories is they take the fun parts of ASoIaF and present them without all the emotional and political baggage. Don’t get me wrong, there’s still some tense moments and a bit of grit here or there, but the ratio is skewed to give the reader a lighter reading experience.<br /><br />I enjoyed getting bits of information on the world in these stories. There’s references to familiar families, we get a bit more information on dragons eggs, and learn about a different style of trial by combat than I remember hearing about in ASoIaF. Are any of these the least bit necessary for ASoIaF? Absolutely not. But did I enjoy learning about them and feeling I have a bit more of an understanding? Absolutely.<br /><br />These are all independent short stories, though reading the The Hedge Knight first I think is very important as it reveals who exactly Dunk and Egg are and how they came to travel together. For fans of ASoIaF, particularly readers that are fans of any of Martins duos, I highly recommend it. If for no other reason than they are something enjoyable to read while we wait for Winds of Winter.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16214481677208739623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('q6m+kgud8TuMg4Dl3gLEJTuIaTw9Si5oKOuzP6B6GreuYqn1GJlyo8sZ065fjounKfRJJ39f/7GihgzpCYMNGA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f9NaNP66xmVse5ygjgFQcDuNyCNkEblTVDjSZVwUa/p6GE1T7b5F/Svhz+sPjR/yKfHoOCYEaIreVW2z9e18VQ==')})
  }
//]]>

The story of the creation of the world and of the the First Age, this is the ancient drama to which the characters in THE LORD OF THE RINGS look back and in whose events some of them, such as Elrond and Galadriel, took part. The three Silmarils were jewels created by Feanor, most gifted of the Elves. Within them was imprisoned the Light of the Two Trees of Valinor before the Trees themselves were destroyed by Morgoth, the first Dark Lord. Thereafter, the unsullied Light of Valinor lived on only in the Silmarils, but they were seized by Morgoth and set in his crown, which was guarded in the impenetrable fortress of Angband in the north of Middle-earth. THE SILMARILLION is the history of the rebellion of Feanor and his kindred against the gods, their exile from Valinor and return to Middle-earth, and their war, hopeless despite all their heroism, against the great Enemy.\nThis second edition features a letter written by J.R.R.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin">About George R.R. Martin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_111x148-e08b4682eea7088f8cdfd67c131d51cd.png);'></div>

<a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin">George R.R. Martin

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15167838399407237889">George Raymond Richard "R.R." Martin was born September 20, 1948, in Bayonne, New Jersey. His father was Raymond Collins Martin, a longshoreman, and his mother was Margaret Brady Martin. He has two sisters, Darleen Martin Lapinski and Janet Martin Patten. <br/><br/>Martin attended Mary Jane Donohoe School and Marist High School. He began writing very young, selling monster stories to other neighborhood chil</span>
  <span id="freeText15167838399407237889" style="display:none">George Raymond Richard "R.R." Martin was born September 20, 1948, in Bayonne, New Jersey. His father was Raymond Collins Martin, a longshoreman, and his mother was Margaret Brady Martin. He has two sisters, Darleen Martin Lapinski and Janet Martin Patten. <br /><br />Martin attended Mary Jane Donohoe School and Marist High School. He began writing very young, selling monster stories to other neighborhood children for pennies, dramatic readings included. Later he became a comic book fan and collector in high school, and began to write fiction for comic fanzines (amateur fan magazines). Martin's first professional sale was made in 1970 at age 21: "The Hero," sold to Galaxy, published in February, 1971 issue. Other sales followed. <br /><br />In 1970 Martin received a B.S. in Journalism from Northwestern University, Evanston, Illinois, graduating summa cum laude. He went on to complete a M.S. in Journalism in 1971, also from Northwestern. <br /><br />As a conscientious objector, Martin did alternative service 1972-1974 with VISTA, attached to Cook County Legal Assistance Foundation. He also directed chess tournaments for the Continental Chess Association from 1973-1976, and was a Journalism instructor at Clarke College, Dubuque, Iowa, from 1976-1978. He wrote part-time throughout the 1970s while working as a VISTA Volunteer, chess director, and teacher. <br /><br />In 1975 he married Gale Burnick. They divorced in 1979, with no children. Martin became a full-time writer in 1979. He was writer-in-residence at Clarke College from 1978-79. <br /><br />Moving on to Hollywood, Martin signed on as a story editor for Twilight Zone at CBS Television in 1986. In 1987 Martin became an Executive Story Consultant for Beauty and the Beast at CBS. In 1988 he became a Producer for Beauty and the Beast, then in 1989 moved up to Co-Supervising Producer. He was Executive Producer for Doorways, a pilot which he wrote for Columbia Pictures Television, which was filmed during 1992-93. <br /><br />Martin's present home is Santa Fe, New Mexico. He is a member of Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy Writers of America (he was South-Central Regional Director 1977-1979, and Vice President 1996-1998), and of Writers' Guild of America, West. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/georgerrmartin">http://us.macmillan.com/author/george...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15167838399407237889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
